D. Analysis of Water Supply Resources in Jinan
At present, the water supply resources are groundwater, reservoir water and
Yellow River water which are analyzed in detail below.
a) Groundwater
Considering Jinan as a famous spring city, the spring spraying should be
guaranteed when extracting groundwater. According to calculation, the range from
300,000 tld to 420,000 t/d is rational with spring spraying at the rate of 85,0(X) -
120,000 tld.
b) Reservoir Water
After Wohushan and Jinixiuchuan reservoir project are extended. the amount of
water supply will reach 150,000 t/d.
c) Yellow River Water
The Yellow River runs into Jinan west from Pingyin county to east Fanjiavuan,
Zhangqiu county with a total line 172.9 Km. This gives an advantage of using
Yellow River water. Based on the analysis predication of Yellow River water, the
water amount in the follow years is: 8.25 billion cubic meter in 2000, 6.7 billion
cubic meter per year in 2020. So it is possible to use Yellow River water resources
before 2020 if the project is made in order.
d) The Action of Abstraction from West to East
4-23



It is a large water supply project to use the water of Dongping lake wlhich
pondaged from Changjiang River, Yellow River and Hanjiang River. If this project is
completed, 200 million cubic meter would send to Jinan every year. So it is a main
water supply resources in the future.
E. Impacts Analysis of Abstraction from Queshan Pondage Reservoir on
Groundwater Environment
From the Table 6.1.15, it may be found that with the economic development
and population increase of Jinan city, the amount of water demand and drainage
becomes larger and larger. However, there are only three main water resources in
Jinan - ground water reservoir water and Yellow river water, meanwhile the water
supply of reservoir is very limited. So the only method to get water supply should
over-extract ground water if the Yellow River water isn't uscd. C)bviouisly, over-
extracting will mak-e serious results, such as the level of groundwater decreasing, no
spraying of Baotu spring, bad influence of Jinan natural landscape and the indirect
influence the tourism. Moreover, over-extracting will cause to water supply shiortage
of Daming lake and Xiaoqing river. This will hinder the realization of the aim to V-
class which the water quality will reach the "The quality standard (GB3838-88) of
ground water in 2000". Thus it is very useful for maintaining both groundwater level
and spring landscape and it can also improve the groundwater quality afler extracting
Yellow River water.
4.1.3.2.6 The Impact Analysis of Slit Produce(d in the Plrocess ofY ellow River
Water Purifying on Environment
In the whole purifI,ing process, silt comes from three sources:(a) the depositing
tank of the first plant; (b) the inclined-tube depositing tank of the second plant; (c)
the two-valve filter tankl of the second plant. The sill produccd by inclinedl-tube
depositing tank, and two-valve filter tank of second plant is drained off to the sewage
tank, then sent to the water distribution by sewage pump of the first plant. finally
processed alter combining with Yellow River water. Ilicrclorc, therC is no bad
influence of the fifth from incline-tube depositing tank and two-valve flter tank on
the surround environment. The silt produced by the depositing tank- of the first water
plant is drained off to the salinization zone. At last, sewage will be separated fiom the
silt by natural depositing and sent to the drainage canal. The silt could be used to
strength Yellow River dam when the height and wvidth reach the planned size, soil
will be chose to cover the silt and it couldn't make any worse effect.

C. The Impact after Completion of Xiaolangdi Reservoir
Xiaolangdi reservoir locates in the lower reaches of SanmerLxia reservoir. From the
calculation result of relative department, after the completion of the Xiaolangdi reservoir,
there is no need to use the retarding basin if the scale of flood is emerged once every one
thousand years. If the scale of flood like that of in 1958 or 1982, after the retarding flood
of Xiaolangdi, the flow in Huayuankou will be reduced from 22,300 to 9,600 m3/s and
15,300 to 8,700 m3/s. So the flood will not exceed the safe limit of river channel in lower
reaches. If there is a catastrophic flood once every ten thousands years, after reduction of
Xiaolangdi and reservoirs in its upper reaches, the flow in the site of Hu3yua3nkou will be
reduced from 41,700 to 27,350 m3/s, then by means of diversion of retarding basin , the
flow in Aishan will not exceed 10,000 m3/s. Due to the rise of river bed in recent years,
continuing increase of the water level under the same flow compared witll previous years,
the capacity of flood discharge will decrease. Though the completion of Xiaolangdi
reservoir has the function of retaining flood, the flow will probablv exceed the safe limit.
So the possibility using stretch zone for flood diversion will still exist if there is a
extraordinary flood.
So we can draw the conclusion that the normal flood will not have great impact on
the Queshan reservoir. if there is a extraordinary flood, the using of strctch zone lor
flood discharge will have certain impact on the reservoir.

c) Impact from Digestion of Pollutants in Reservoir' s Bed
We cite expert's results from Research on Water Quaity Forecast and Management
Planning and Reservoir and its Environment' Impact (USSR). They think- that the
fifteenth day after pondage of the reservoir is the peak-hour of digestion of pollutants in
reservoir's bed. It is proven from static simulation test that afler three to fottr times of
water circulation, the impact of pollutants' digestion can be omitted. Moreover, about 10
% of sands in the Yellow River's water will be settled in reservoir' s bed. After five years,
this kind of impact can also be omitted. According to the dead capacity of 7 million cubic
meter, in the inception stage pondage, the digestion can be omitted if we take the
measure such as washing the substrate sludge.
d) Impact of Agricultural Activities on Water Quality
Because there are farmlands around the reservoir, the likely impact of agricultural
activities on the reservoir is the spraying of agricultural chemicals and using of chemical
fertilizers during the growth period of crops.
0 Impact of Spraying Agricultural Chemicals
Organic phosphorus chemicals such as Azodrin, Rogor or 1605 are sprayed
from April to October. According to the drift test of agricultural chemicaLs in
Research on Water Quality, Forecast and Management Planning. when 1he wvincd
speed is up to 5.4 m:s, the maximum drift distance and altitude are 20 and 2.5
4-28



meters, respectively ( the agricultural chemicals should be sprayed w-hen the w-id
speed is smaller than 5.4 mis). Because the height of dam is ten meters higLh and a
anti-penetration dike being built, the agiicultural chemicals will not alfec thde water
quality in the reservoir.
* Impact of Spraving Chemical Fertilizers
In 1995, the total amount of chemical fertilizers used in the project area wvere up
to 3,796 tons, including 2,228 tons of nitrogen. 1,344 tons of phosphorms. From the
analysis of using period and method of chemical fertilizers, comparinig the height of
dam and farmlands, the function of anti-penetration dike, we know the using of
chemical fertilizers will not affect the water quality in the reservoir.
After the operation of the reservoir, the main factors affecting the water quality are
water quality in Yellow River, rainfall and dust fall. The amount of total nitrogen and
total phosphorus brought about by rainfall and dust fall are 0.83∞o and 18.14%0 of that
caused by Yellow River, respectively. The using of agricultural and chemical fertilizers
will not affect the water qualitv in the reservoir. With respect to the impact of dioestion
from reservoir's bed, after three or four times of water circulation, it can be omitted. So
if we take measures like washing before operation of the reservoir, there ivill be no
impact from the digestion from reservoir's bed.
B. Trend Anal-sis of Water Pollution in the Resenroir
The pollutants in the reservoir are mainly from Yellow River. rainfall andl dust fall.
With respect to Yellow River, because its river bed is much higher thanl average
height of ground and assimilating capability of sands in the river. thte water qualitv in
Yellow River will be in a stable state.
In terms of pollution from rainfall and dust fall. the impact is very snmall Cxcclt tIlat
caused by total nitrogcn and total phosphorus.
From the analysis above, we know that the factors affected the water quality in
reservoir are in a stable state. In addition. The planning supply and use are fundamental
balance. The period of water remaining in the reservoir is relatively slhort because the
water recvcles once a vear, this will be helpful to the water quality's stability.
4.1.3.3.3 Analvsis and Forecast ot Queshan Resen'oir's W ater Quality antd

If the reservoir accepts excessive nutrient substances, the alga and other water
plants will be overbreeding, which will cause the dissolved oxygen in the waler bodlv
reduced greatly and deterioration of water quality.
We selected the Pucheng Reservoir as analogous investigation objectivc to forecast
the possibility and development trend of eutrophication.

total phosphorus, transparency are 3.33, 0.32, 0.028 mg/I, 0.46 ni, respectively. The
main types of plankton alga are blue green alga and diatom. The water quality is between
middle and eutrophic type.

B. Forecast of Nitrogen's and Phosphorus's Concentration in Queshan Reservoir
Nitrogen and phosphorus are the most important indexes inrdicating the
eutrophication extent of the reservoir. So, Finding out the input, output and
accumulating volume of nitrogen and phosphorus has important meaning for forecasting
and prevention the eutrophication in the reservoir.
a) Calculation of Nitrogen's and Phosphorus's Balance in the Reservoir
From the analysis of chapters above, we know the annual input volume of nitrogen
and phosphorus are 808.77 and 12.05 tons, respectively.
The annual supply amount to Jinan city of the reservoir is 156.07 miUion cubic
meters with the seepage loss of 3.93 million cubic meters. So, the accumulation amount
of nitrogen and phosphorus are 28.77 and 2.13 tons, respectively.
The results are calculated by monitoring data just after dry-up of Yellow River on
July, 8, 1996, as we discussed above, it is not the normal period for abstraction. For
remedying the defects of the data, we utilize the aver age value of routine monitoring data

respectively. The accumulation amount of nitrogen and phosphorus are 2.01 and 0.2
tons, respectively.

2) Pipelines
The project's pipeline network, is consisted of the renovated pipelines and the
newly-built pipelines. See Table 4.2.2 for details. 1lhe waste water network includes only

For the communities under construction and to be constructed , laing of their
waste water disclharge branch pies will take place togetlher with the comnnuities'
construction. All branch pipes will be planned and monitored by the Municipal
Construction Bureau. Pipelines for enterprises' special use will be connected by the
enterprises thcmselves according to municipal administration's requirements.
3) Waste Water Pump Stations
Jiluoqiao pump station was built in 1987, and is presently in good condition. There
is no need for enlargement since its future operation is only 181.3 thousand m3/d.
North and south Lishan Streets main pipeline and Darning Lake Road main pipeline
meet at Lihuang Road Cross, and then go northward through Lihuang Road railroad
flyover. A D1600 waste water pipe has already been laid beneath the railroad flyover
whose elevation is very low. Therefore the upperstream main pipes can bc directly
44-40



connected in, which makes the Daning Lake punp station obsolescent.
A new punp station whose designed capacity is 100 thousand m3/d will be built at
the cross of Lihuang Road and Beiyuan Road to pump the waste water from the soutI.
The present Lishan Road pump station will fall into disuse.
4.2.1.2.8 Project Investment
Investrnent for this urban sewerage network- project will be 256.95 million yuan.
According to World Bank's requirement, given factors like price rise, etc., the total
investment is estimated to be 282.65 million yuan, in which 155.15 million yuan is
domestic fuids, and 127.5 million yuan from World Bank loans (about 15 million
USD).

4.2.1.3.2 Coordination of the Project, Waste Water Discharge Sources and Waste Water
Treatment Plants
The sewerage network project will be started on May 1, 1997 with a construction
period of 4 years, and is to be finished in 2000. The waste water treatment plants vill be
in normal operation. By that time, the urban waste water amount will be 1460 thousand
m3ld, and Jinan Waste water Treatment Plant's coverage will be 482 thousand m3/d.
But its actual treatment amount is only 220 thousand m31d with the rest 262 thousand
m3/d being discharged directly into Xiaoqing River. In 2010, the total waste water
amount of the 4 systemLs within the network's confluence scope will be 579.1 thousand
n3d. The waste water treatment plant will still be insufficient to meet the network's
capacity. Therefore, the II-phase of the project of Gejiagou Waste water Treatment
Plant should be quickened. Jinan Waste water Treatment Plant's II-phase construction
has a treatment capacity of 230 thousand m3/d, and its total treatment capacity of 1-
phase and lI-phase is designed to be 450 thousand m31d.
There will still be 129.1 thousand m3/d to be discharged into Xiaoqing River.
Thercfore, to reduce waste water discharge, strict measures should be taken to control
the main polluting sources, close some hard-to-manage enterprises, innovate production
4-42



techniques, save and reuse water, etc. in order to mitigate the pollution in Xiaoqing
River.
4.2.1.4 Economic Feasibility Analvsis of the Project
Action plan of Jinan urban sewerage networlk project is compiled on the Iollowing
principles:
*  designed for a far future, the year 2010;
*  compiled on the basis of Jinan Gejiagou Waste Water Treatment Plant main pipes
system layout;
*  adopted rain-waste water diffluence to control water bod) pollution effectivey,;
*  on the basis of the existing pipelines, taking into account the connection with Jinan
Waste Water Treatment Plant's imported pipes;
*  taking advantages of terrains to discharge downward, minimising the number of
pump stations;
*  pipelines arranged to take in all the waste water; Newly laid pipes are first to
discharge the areas with large amount of waste water, poor water quality or other
situations of urgency;
*  When the original pipe is found not thick enough, to build a new one should be
firstly considered. Where it is hard to widen a road and there is no place for a new
pipe, renovation of the original pipe should be considered.
Based on the above-mentioned principles, this prQject has the following features:
4.2.1.4.1 Small Work Amount, Low Investment
I   The project basically makes use of the existing pipes. Total work amount of Ihe
project includes 50.9 km's renovated and newly-built pipelines, 1.5 km of newly-built
inverted siphon pipes, a newly-built pump station, 235.37 mu of land acquisition and
58725 m2 of dismantling area. Basic investment of the project is only 256.95 Imillion
yuan, much less than the usual investmcnt ratio of sewerane network; and waste wiler
treatment plant.
4.2.1.4.2 Low Operation Fund
The project takes advantage of the natural terrains and the existing pipeline
elevation. Therefore only one new pump station is needed for the nen network and one
preserved, which greatly reduces the fiuture operation maintenance 1ees.
4.2.1.4.3 Significant Envirornental Benefits
1) Small Environmental Impact During the Construction Period
Except the two main pipes in Darming Lake system which entail a fuill-length
pipeline renovation and new construction, the pipelines in other svsienims are Sparsely
situated
at parts of different roads, which will restrict environmental impact into limited areas. In



line with the overall planning, the project's pipe-laying and construction will be
simultaneous. Overhead pipe-laying will be adopted at suitable places in or-der lo mitigate
the environmental impact on the neighborliood.
2) Significant enviionmental benefits after completion of the project
On completion of the project, Jinan's urban infrastructure will be strengthened,
urban water quality will be radically improved and pollution in Xiaoqing River will be
greatly mitigated, which will guarantee a great improvement in the urban enmironxnent.
Therefore, the project is feasible both technologically and economically.
For detail description, see Project Environmental Impact Analysis Report.
4.2.1.5 Analysis of Project's Environmental lmpact Factors
The network construction is a big project for the urban and industrial waste wvater
to be transported to and treated by Jinan Waste water Treatment Plant. It is a project for
pollution control environment protection, city beautification and improvement of urban
infrastructure. However, as a construction item, during its construction and operation, it
will inevitably bring about some impact on its surroundings, and may even bring about
some changes in the city's overall planning. Analyses are made in the followvine three
aspects.
4.2.1.5.1 Analysis of the Project's Impact on the Social Environment
The project will bring about many impacts oni the social environment, degree,
scope and duration of impacts being different and complicated. To solve the main
problems, five aspects to be affected have been decided according to experts'
consultation and technical analysis wvhich are urbali transportation, urban population,
flood prevention and discharge, urban green lands and the original underground network.
wilh the first 3 aspects to be affected nmost seriously.
1) Project's Impact on Urban Transportation
The projcct involves 24 streets within the coverage scope with a total lcngtlh of 49
km. Except that two main pipelines are laid along both sides of Tiancheng Road, other
streets are all single-pipeline laying. Most main pipes of the project are form south to
nortlh; east-to-west pipelincs are mostly branchi pipes, most of wlhich arc short and affect
only a small area.
Newly-built and renovated pipelines mtostly locate witlin the urban area, which
will bring about certain impact on urban transportation durino construetion. Biggest
impacts on urban transportation exist on the following 4 roads.
a. From south ring road northward to Yingxiongshan Road to Weier Roa( to Tiancheng
Road to Jiluo Road to north ring road, wlhich is Jinan's transportation aorta.
b. From south ring road northward to Yulhan Road to Qingnian West Road to Wenhua
West Road to Shunhe Street to Shenochan Road to Qinghe Road to Yan-hu Road on

the north bank of Xiaoqing River.
c. From Shungeng Road northward lo Qingnian East Road to Chaoshan Street 1o Xianxi
Alley to Darning Lake Road to Lishan Street to Lihtuang Road to East Luohle Road
to Xiaoqing River.
d. Parts of Lishan North Road and Shanida Road.
Irnpact on the above-mentioned roads during construction chiefly rests in tiie traflic
increase on their adjacent roads. Traffic jams may occur on some of the roads.
To reduce traffic pressurc and improve the roads' traffic capacity, stricter measures
should be taken on traffic management, vehicle dispatchment and bus line adjustment.
Construction is to take place peniodically and separately on a reasonable schedule.
Biggest mutual impact occurs on the tow main pipeline construction in Jiluo Road
system and Darning Lake Road system. Presently, Jinan is planning to build a flvover
along the Daming Lake system. The construction of this flyover conisists of 2 plhases.
The first phase is from Qingnian West Road to Shunhe Street to Jingshi Road Cross to

pressure brought about by construction.
2) Project's Impact on Urban Population
The project entails a land acquisition of 235.37 mu, most of which arc old roads,
residential area and enterprises' land. It involves a dismantling area of 31280 m2, 310
farnilies and 84 cntcrpriscs. Population afIfcted hits 1460. Migration and settlcincnt foe
comes up to 64.7945 million yuan. It is planned that local and migrant settlement be
adopted.
3) Project's Impact on Flood Prevention and Flood Discharge
Jinan's rainwater discharge system makes it possible for the rainlwater to be
discharged into the nearest river course and finalhl into Xiaoqing River. The main
flood-discharge ditches in the system are renovated natural river courses.
Xiaoqing River is Jinan's chief flood-discharge channetl but its capacity is pretty
low and is onlv able to deal with a flood ever' 5 years. Xiaoclino River's brinclhes wilhin
the coverage scope, which either flow into or are pumped into Xiaoqing River. have also
pretty low capacities, handling floods event 20 to 50 y ears.
Pipelines in the network project are mostlv laid along the streets. so there will not be
mnany crosses with flood-disclharge ditches. For tlhe few which do entail crossings,
overhead inverted siphon pipes will be adopted, so the project will not bring about any
impact on the city's flood-discharge svstem. Only at Shunhie Street part where Xiweizi
Ditch will be covered up owing to the construction of the flvover, flood-prevention
requirements should be taken into consideration in waste water pipeline laving. It will be
better for the construction to take place duriig the ditch's dry-up period and oii a high
level of flood-prevention capacity.

5) Project's Impact on the Old Underground Networl

4.2.1.5.2 Analysis of Project's Environmnental Impact Factors
The project's environmental impact factors include: surface water, gounid water,
noise and dust during construction. According to I'OR. surface water, ground water and
noise are the key factors. Analyses of the 4 above-mentioned factors fuollow.
1) Analysis of the Project's Impact on Surface Water
The network project has 4 systems to transport Jinan City's waste water to Jinan
Waste water Treatment Plant. The plant's I-phase capacitv is 22(0 thousand mT/d. but is
not in use since the network has not been built yel. After completion of tihe network
project, the waste water presently discharged into thc river courses will be sent through
pipes into Xiaoqing River blank pipes, 220 thousand m3/d of the waste water will be
treated by the waste water treatment plant first, and then discharged into Xiaoqing River.
The rest will be discharged directly into the river. On the one hand, the waste wvater will
not be discharged into the urban river courses, so the pollution in Gonosliang River,
Dongluo River, ,iluo River and Liuhangtou River wvill be cffectivewl controlled, and
Darning Lake will retrieve its former beautv. On the other hand. since the 220 thouisand
m3/d waste water is treat4d, quantitv of pollutants in Xiaoqing River will be greatly
reduced: reduction of COD 88t/d, BOD 53t1d, SS 81td, which contributes greatly to tlhe
comprehensive treatmcnt of Xiaoqing, River.
2) Analysis of the Project's Inpact on Ground WNater
After the completion of the project, the quality of the surlace waler in ihe rivers and
lakes within the covcragc scopc will be improved, and thc pollution caused by the
leakage from surface water to ground water will be mitigated. On the other hand, the
waste water network, covers a big area and many streets, so leakage in waste waler
conveying will be the main polluting source afier the complction of the project.
Since tubewell drainage technique is adopted in the network construction. gromnd
4 -41l



water level for certain areas will be affected, which will cause ground water loss and
ground water level decrease. Therefore, during construction, measures should be taken
to enhance the quality, of construction, like the joint of pipes, invertcd siphion pipes, etc.,
and to quicken construction speed in order to mitigate the impact caused this way.
3) Analysis of Project's Noise and Dust dutring Construction
lhe project is a large-scale infrastructure construction item which involves a big
construction area, lots of vehicles and machines, big carthwork- and a large construction
population. The construction vehicles and machines will be the chief polluting sources of
noise and dust, like digging, piling, concrete mixing, earth-conveying, road-rolling, etc.
Besides, since the construction sites are usually closed or half closed to traffic,
indirect noise and dust pollution may last for the whole conistruction period owing to the
increase of traffic in the neighboring area. Ilowever, it will cease on completioni of tlhe.
project.
To mitigate noise and dust pollution. stricter measures should be taken to enhlance
construction management. Construction is to be planned into separatc phascs on a
reasonable schedule. Construction vehicles and machines should be used at a time when
minimum impact on the neighborhood is possible. Spccial roads and special traffic time
should be arranged for the construction vehicles. Special trucks arc to transport the
surplus earth to designative places outside the citv in time. Construction sites are to be
clcaned up in lime when construction ceases. Advancedi maclhines will be used.
Construction speed is to be raised. And the construction period is to be shortened.
Efforts will be made to mitigate the project's impact in time, space and degree.
4.2.1.5.3 Project's Impact on Overall Planning
The action plan for Jinan Urban Waste Water Netwvork is compiled according to
Jinan City's overall planning, on the basis of Jinan Gcjiagou Wl7aste water T'reatment
Plant's Main Pipeline System Lavout in 1989. During the compilation of the action plan.
coordination of different factors was given full consideration. Present existing pipelines
have been used to the utmost. Pipelines are laid at designative roads, with only a few to
be widened. The whole network falls into the 4 systems, with a renovated pipelile lengtlh
of 7A4 km, a ncwly-built pipeline length of 43.5 km, a total of 50.9 km along the existing
designative roads. Therefore the project will not bring ahout too much impact to the
city's overall planning.
4.2.1.5.4 Analvsis of Project's Impact on Ecological Restoration
'I1is network- project is botlh an urban public facility anid anl onviiomuetital
protection facility. After completion of the project, ecological environment will be
restored to a certain degree.
a. Water quality of Xiaoqing River will bc greatly bettered. Worsening of the ecological
system will be checked. For many years, pollution in Xiaoqing River has brought
abouL the changes in the river's water conditions, ecological balance being shattered.
With the waste watcr network being put in use, Xiaoqing River's ccology will be
restored to some degree. and the agricultural ecology will develop in thie direction of



beneficial circulation. Xiaoqing River has been irrigating its neighboring farmlands
for 35 years, the pollutants migrating into the agricultural ecological system. The
waste water network will greatly mitigate the pollution in this point and the land
vegetation and ecology will be improved greatly. Besides, the fishenr production in
Laizhou Bay will also improve since Xiaoqing River flows into the sea there. lost
of all, Xiaoqing River inhabitants' health wil be guaranteed.
b. Jinan is known as the "Spring City" which is famous for its 72 springs with Darning
Lake like a pearl in the city. However, water pollution has badly damaged Jinan's
tourism. Due to too much inflow of the urban domestic waste water, the original clear
lake has been badly polluted with organic matters and been overnutritious, consuming
lots of dissolved oxygen. River courses in the city, like Gongshang River, Dongluo
River, XiJuo River, Liuhangtou River, Weizi Ditch. etc., have become waste water-
dischlarge ditclhes, smelly and sludgy all year rounid, vhich greatly damages thle city's
environment. After completion of the project, urban waste water will be sent to the
waste water treatment plant through a complete pipeline network, pollution in urban
livers, lakes, springs, etc., obviated; thus the tourism rcsourecs wiU be protcctcd
effectively and "Spring City" will keep its name forever, and the Daming "Pearl" will
shine again.

Above all, ground water quality in this area is generally good, and karst water is

southeast part of the urban area, which means that the ground water conditions there are
sensitive and should be protected particulariy.
4.2.3.1.2  Ground Water Environmental Impact Analysis
Operation of Jinan Urban Waste Water Network will bring about great impact on
urban ground water conditions. The impact lie in the following aspects.
1) Impact during Construction
During construction, plenty of digging work must he done to bun, the pipes. And
the deeper the pipes are to be buied, the more digging work is necessary. Two
possibilities exist to cause negative impact on ground water.
a. South of Jingshi Road, in Jingshanzhuang, Yangtouyu, Nanjiao Hotel, Yingxiongshan
mountain areas, limestone are shallow or even exposed. Tllirefore, local explosioi
is necessary for pipe-laying. Dynammon will bring about NOx pollution to ground
water. The degree of pollution is in direct relation to the explosive amount and
development of limestone rockholes. The more explosive is used, and the more
developed the rockholes are, the worse the pollution will be. But, this kind of
ground water pollution will be. But, this kind of pollution will only cause the
degradation of water quality, not of the water's function.
b. During old network renovation, the formed sedimental layer of sludge on the bottom
of the waste water discharge ditches havc to be digged up again, which makes it
easier for the waste water to percolate underground, causing an increase in
percolation within short period of time. So, during renovation, like Yuhan Road,
Weier Road, Shengohang Road, had better take place during dry-up peniod to
minimize waste water percolation.
2) Inpact on Ground Water When the Network is in Use
a. Positive Impact on Ground Water When the Network is in Use
When the network- is in use, waste water will be discharged through pipes instead of
ditches, and will flow into waste water plant for treatment, which will greatly reduce the
waste water percolalion supplement to ground water. At present, waste water is
discharged mainly through ditches.
Since the ditch bottoms have vern good perviousness, especiaDly in the south and
southeast parts of the urban area where limestone is shallow or even exposed, waste
water is sure to percolate down, causing pollution to underground water. Due to lack of
systematic monitoring materials and relevant data, there is no way to calculate this
percolation amount. But bascd on the analysis of waste water dischargc ditches,
geological structure and the present underground water conditions, waste water
percolation is sure to have happened. Influenced by waste waler percolation, Jinan urban
rockhole water quality is generally very poor, and karst ground water quality has also
been affected.
4-62



When the network takes the place of discharge ditches, waste water percolation will
be avoided and ground water conditions and quality will also be bettered. It will bring
about the most obvious impact on rockhole water and karst water will also be favorably
influenced. Present karst water pollution will be hindered.
b. Negative Impact on Ground Water Wlhen the Network is in Use.
Negative impact on ground water lies in the waste water leakage caused by pipe
breakage, pipe joints or shaft inverted siphon pipes. The leakage will bring about ground
water pollution. If the pipeline position is near the original dischargc ditch, then the
leakage will not aggravate ground water pollution. But if the pipes are laid where there
are no discharge ditches like the east part of Beiyuan Road, new local pollution will
occur. The pollution will be more obvious, especially at places where the rock
perviousness is good, like most of the newly-built network area north of Xiaoqing River.
4.2.3.2 Measures Taken to Prevent Ground Water Pollution
Operation of Jinan waste water pipeline network will protect and improve the urban
ground water conditions. However, pipeline digging and burying, and waste water runoff,
overflowing, dripping and leaking will bring about ground water pollution. Since there
are too big differences in hydrophite types, Quaternry Period thickness, aerated area's
lithology and leakage prevention, ground water will be divided up into different areas
according to its sensitivity, no tlhat corresponding protection measures may be taken.
And, protection measures will also be taken in project design and the construction
peiod.
4.2.3.2.1 Ground Water Sensitive Area Division
Jinan locates on the joint of Taishan mountain's north stretch and its front sloping
plain, and is of a high-south-low-north terrain. The southem low mountains and hills are
500-900m above sea level; the middle hills are 1 00-500m above sea level: the northern
sloping plain is 10-100m above sea level. The work area locates in the middle and iiorai
of the city. Southeast area is tectonic corrosion and corrosion hills. Northwest area is
sloping plain, declining northward, slope declivity being 0.23-0.9%∞. Ditch valleys are
fully developed.
Exposed seralum in the area i5. mainly composed of Ordovician, Quaternary Period
and Yanshlan period magma rock. See Fig 4.2.5 for the network area's Hy&dogeological
conditions. GCound water sensitive area can be divided into 3 kinds according to surface
lithology, Quaternarv Period thickness. aerated area's leakage prevention and low-hin2
hydrophite types, etc., that is, grounid water enviroiuient very sensitive area (1), grouInd
water environment sensitive area (II), and ground water environmtent non-sensitive area
(DII). Detailed description follow.
a. Ground Water Environment Very Scnsitivw Aeca (I)
This area locates in the southern area of the city, which is the area south of the
igneous rockbody's southern boundary line, including Jingshanzhuang, Yangtouyu,
Qianfoshan mountain, Baotu Spring, Heihlu Spring. Baliwa, Yinxiongshan mountain, etc.
The karst ground water is supplemented in the southem mountain area ( out of this area),
4-63



and then flows into this area. It is blocked by the nollhern rock body. so springs form
when water level is raised above the ground level. This area is rich in karst ground water.
It is an important source for Jinan urban water supplv. and a place where most famious
springs locate.
In this area, hydrolith bodi is exposed or shallowhy buried. In the cxposcd area.
karst crevices are filUy developed with good perviousness and thus poor waste water
percolation prevention capacity. So this area's environmental condition is very sensitive.
In this area, even small amount of low density pollutants will percolate into the hvdrolith
layer, causqig pollution. Therefore, this area is categorized into the very sensitive area
due to its social function and its poor self-protection ability.
b. Ground Water Environment Sensitive Area
This is the area north of Xiaoqing River, where the Quatemary Period thickness is
mostly more than 30m and creviced hydrolith bodv is fulls developed. It has some water
supply capability. Its surface litholog; is mainly of fine sands and sandv loam. So this
area has good perviousness, and thus poor waste water percolation prevention capability.
Therefore, it is categorized into the senLsitive area.
c. Ground Wl'ater Environrment Non-sensitive Area (III)
This area locates in the wor;k area, fiom .linan's old urban area to Qilihe in the east.
where Quatematy Period thickness is 10-3()m. and( litliology is mainly laiii. carth lam.
and sandy loam. Surface layer of this area does not have good water-containing rock
body. Undemeath is the igneous rock bodv, so the whole area is of little value in water
supplv. Although the low-lying aerated laxer (lam.n earth lam. sands loam) has good
perviousness, percolation of pollutants in this area will not bring about amy apparent
impact on water supplv and springs. Therefore, this area is categorized into the. non-
sensitive area.
4.2.3.2.2 Ground Water Environmental Protection Area Dixision
a. Karst Ground Water Kev Protection Arca (I)
This is the ground water envronment very sensitive area (1). In this area, great
attention must be paid to ground water enmironmental protection. Firstly. in city planning
and industry arTangement, this area should be listed as thc cultuiai atrea and( scenic
tourism area. where polluting enterprises and urban garbage pileup are prohibited.
Secondly, stlict manaoement should b.e administered on domestic waste water anid
garbage disposal. Domestic waste water should be discharged through the pipeline
network. Discharging into natural ditches is prohibited. Furthermore, large amoutnt of
human manure used in vegetable growing will cause N03, N02, N1H44 and colihacillus
pollution to ground water, so the scale of vegetable growing should also he propcrly
controlled.
b. Crevice Ground Water Key Protection Area (I1)
This is the ground water environment sensitive area (11). T his area can hc platwued
into thc industrial area and the living arac, but waste water miust be discharged tlhrough
the pipeline network. And management of the networkl should be improved to reduce
possible leakage of waste water water. According to design, the rework can basically
meet the need. However, with the expansion of the city, the network's ser se coverage



scope should aLso be enlarged, especially in tlc noilliern line sand area neal the Yellow
River. The whole urban area should be within the network-'s service coverage.
c. Crevice Ground Water General Protection Area (H1)
This is the ground water environment non-sensitive area (Im). Since this area does
not have good water-containing lavers and is of little valuc to waler supply.
environmental protection work in this area can be centiered on ground surface
environmental protection. This does not mean environmental protection of this area's
ground water can be ignored. Pollution should be avoided of the southem karst ground
water and northern cre-ice giound water bv this area's polluted water produced by
strong mining.

environment because of working in 10 m deep ivell.

investigated the equipment, pattem and work-rest schedule of construction in detail in
order to make clear the influence of construction noise. At the same time we inspected
the construction spot in Lihuang Road and measured voice source, so we got a clear
understanding of noise pollution of construction. Excavation and top pipe patterns will
be adopted in planned object. In general, noise pollution of excavation pattem is heavier
while that of top pipe pattem is lighter.

4.2.5 Land Requisition and Dismantling
4.2.5.1 Quantity of Land Requisition and Dismantling
The land requisition and dismantling concem 1460 people, 83 enterprises and 1
school. 235.37 mu land will be conscripted and 310 families will have to move. Area of
dismantled house is 31280m2.
4.2.5.2 Compensatory Measure for Land Requisition and Dismantling
It is estimated that the total area of requisitioned land is 235.37 mu and the cost is
14655.4 thousand yuan while the total area of dismantling house is 31280 m2 and the
cost is 50140.5 thousand yuan. Then the total compensatorn cost for land requisition and
dismantling is 64794.5 thousand yuan.
310 families have to moved, most of which will suffer loss in different degree.
About 130 thousand yuan will compensate to each family, in wlich 0(0 Ihousand yuan
i-or settlement cost and 30 thousand yuan for other compensatory cost. Futthermore, the



removed families will be offer with flats. The concerned enterprises and schools wvill be
compensated, too.
4.2.5.3 Specific Safeguard MIeasure
a. Special institution will be established to be in charge of settlement and compensatory
matters during land requisition and dismantling.
b. Through propaganda, increase the transparency of policies, make removed people
realize the irnportance of the project and their living quality will not decline by proper
measure.
c. Removed people can appeal to judicial institution according to china's laws if they
discontent with settlement or compensatory.
In brief, all kinds of social environmental protective measures will be cmployed to
lighten the adverse impacts of land requisition and dismantlng and to ensure the
successful accomplishment of the project.
4.2.5.4 Analysis Conclusion about Social Environmiienital Impacts of Land
Requisition and Dismantling
a. The evaluated area is a conjunctive area of old city and town. Its characteristic of
higher population density, land productivity and fixed asset value result in higher cost
and economic price of the project. But implement of land requisition and dismantling
plan and construction of pipeline network wvill improve living environment and living
quality of residents, including the target people.
b. The impact on social environment of the project mainvly expresses in aspects of
dismantling and settlement, and it is actual. direct and irreversible. The influence is
negative in short-term but positive in long-term to most concerned people. Most of the
concerned people agree wNith inplement of the project because the) can make up their
cost with government compensator) or potential interest of the project.
c. Measures should be taken to enhance social environmental protection and to ensure
that living quality of concerned people will not degrade.

Loan Project Area
Jinan area has hvo loan projects: Jinan Queshan Pondagre Reservoir Prroject {or
drawing Yellow Rivcr to supplv water and Jinani Urban Waste 'Water Networik Project.
There is little relation between two projects, and en-Oronmental itmpacts of each project

In brief, construction of Jinan Queshan Pondagc Resenroir will increase 156 million
tons water supply for Jinan. relax water supply tension of Jinan during dryvup period of

restoring Spring City s spectacle of Jinan. The sewage pipeline network project will
greatly improxe water quality of rivers and lakes and restore the attractive natural

spectacle of Jinan. Its benefit in economy, environment and society is significant.
The construction of projects will probabhl bring some adverse impacts on
environment, but it is temporal. the adverse influence can be lower to bottom by proper
meanings. As long as the Three Synchronization discipline is persisted in project
construction, the influence will be very little, and its positive effect wil be much greater
than the negative one.

5.1.3 General Picture of the Proposed Project
5.1.3.1 Objectives and Scope
The main objectivcs of the PYHN are to:
*  supply CHP heat through district heating in District Zhifu. and thus dismantle the existing
boilers and stoves, so as to improve the air quality,
*  demonstrate how to implement some new technolog) in composition and operation of
district heating (DH) system to reduce its operation coast and increase its reliabiiitv.
*  demonstrate new heating systems to be installed in the consumer's house so that room
temperature can be independently regulatcd an heating bill can be collected according to
the used heat quantity.
5.1.3.2 Scale and Main Counterparts of tne Project
The annual'heat consumption is 3.82x106 GJ/y. The proposed project anid its counterparts
includc: 30.22 km long hot-water network- (Grade 1), 42 heat-exchanger stations. 2 booster
pump stations and one peak load heating boilers (4-;29MW).
5.1.3.3 Investment
The total investment of the proposed project is estimated to be RXIB Yuan 388 million
(USD 46.2 million), in which RMIB Yuan 193.2 million (USD 23.2 million) is the loans from the
World Bank, and the others will be collected domestically.
5.1.3.4 Staffs Arranged
The organization being responsible for construction and implementation of the proposed
proicct if Yantai Heat and Power Office. The present member in the office is about 120, The
staffs in the agencv will be increased gradually to 543 when the operation are in full scale.
5.1.3.5 Heating Area



Area of this project area is 47.4 kmn with population of 400.000, and is expected lo kelc)
the same in 2000. This area is the center of politics, economv and culture in Yantai Citv.
The scope of the proposed project will supply heat to 22 planned block areas (Fig. 5.1.2),
the district heating area will be 8.164 million M2 (actual floor area, the flooing is thc samc).
iincluding most civil and public buildings of District Zihifu. The Municipal Planuing shows that
the 22 block areas will have total building area of 7.72 million m2, including 5.5 million im2 of
civil used  building and 2.22 million mz of public building.
5.1.3.6 Plane Distributioni of the Proposed Project
The proposed project is west to Huang-Bo-Hai Heat and Power Company, east to Putao
Mount, north to the North Road and south to the Qishan Road, as shown in Fig. 5.1.3.
The District Heating Networkl will be 30.22 km long, including a 8.5 km long main line.
The main line will be located above the slope of hillside of the southem hills. skip to the North

5.1.4 Technical Aspects of the Heating System
The technical aspects of heating network and peak load heating boilers' house will be
briefed in this section.
5.1.4.1 On the Heating Network
A. Operation and Adjustment of the Heating Network;
The main heat source of the PYHN is extracted steam from the two 100MW boilers in Line
B of the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat and Power Companv. the steam's parameters are: 0.2047 Mpa
absolute pressure and at temperature of 121 'C. Maximum of steam-extracted is 460t0h, and the
capacity of heat-supply is 1,090.8 GJ/h.
The extracted steam enters the head station, and heats the water in the network b v transfer
heat from steam to water. The heated water enters the secondary heat consumer station, anid is
raised to the required temperature and then sent to consumers. Circulation pumps are installed in
the heat station to withdraw water through the main line, to force it through the heat exchangers
and feed back into the network- again. The technological diagram of the heating Network is
shown in Fig.5.1.4.
The network is divided in to two pan. The part between the head station and the secondary
heat-exchanger station is called Primary Circuit whose water is at 127/60 'C, The palt between
the secondary heat-exchangcr station and consumers is called Secondary Circuit. whose water is
designed to be 80/55 'C. There is no hydraulic relationship between the Primary and Secondarv
Circuit. Fig. 5.1.5 shows the adjustment curves of water temperature.
The temperature of water suppled bv the netNvork is affected b-v the outside temperature,
which also influences on the operation of the peak load heating souI ces.
When outside temperature at 8 to -1.5 IC,the heating-supply load is 1,100 GJih, the
supplicd water tempcraturc remains constant at 1 1 0 'C in Primary C ircuit. T'hc water from head
station can enter the secondarn station and change to suit heating re4uiremenIts.
NNThen outsidc temperature below -1.5 rC, heating-supply load is u) to 1,500 GWI. the flow
will remain constant. However some flow must be raised to 150 ∞C by installing a peak load
heating boiler withi capacitv of 400GJ/li, and then enter the maini circuits and mix witli the
unheated flow  (110 'C) to reach supply temperature of 127 'C.
Under the condition of outside temperature below 6 C, hcating-suppl- load is up to
1,652.42 GJ/h. bevond the heat-supply ability of Power Station and the Peak Load Hleating

B. IIumane and Scenery,
The principle in designing this project is least resettlement and building's destruction. The

social-economical effeGts'is described in " the Report of Analysis of Land Requisition and
ResctLiement's Effect on Society Economy"
The Suochengli Street is planned to be the area of "Old Appearance of the City" by the
M'unicipal Government. Most of buildings in the tvo sides of the Street were built in Ming
Dynlasty, now have an area of 64,000m2, and arc used as resident house and small store. These
buildings will be a little affected in construction phase. So it's suggcsted that this Street should be
dug by manpower so as to avoid the buildings' destruction.
Thete are no Natural Reserve Zone and Wet Land in the construction sites. The trees and
grass along construction sites will be carefully protected, so there is no bad effect on the
ecological environment in construction phase.

Cotntrolling, Noise in Industrial Enterprises )) (GBJ87-85). The noisc is lower than 35dB(A) when
roaching the rcsident areas, witlin the limit of  (( National Enwoviro ental Noise Standard in
Urban Area )>  (GB30G6-93). The staffs in the pump room  are all equipped with noise-
prevolnters.

5.1.7 innovations and Reliability of the Technology
5.1.7.1 A Heating System with Multi-lhcat Sources
In the project, the cogeneration plant acts as the base heat source at the beginning and the
end period of heating season, Temperature raising peak load plant and off-line peak load plants,
are put into operation in tum as heating load increases with drop of outside temperature. Such
heating system can makc the heating-supplier in the ClU-' Station match the Network without any
changes, and also save coal.
5.1.7.2 Primary Network Inicluding Loop Circuit and Branches
Looped routes are arrangod in heavy load dense area to increase the heating reliability.
5.1.7.3 Two Ways of Building Heating Network
In order to lessen the bad effect of network to the greatest extent, Some pipelines are
located above ground and some are buried directly underground.
5.1.7.4 Microcomputer Monitoring System
This system is used to eliminate hydraulic and thermal unbalances, and achieve optimum
operation. The reliability of operation and management of district heating system are thus
irnproved.
5.1.7.5 Thermostatic Valves and Heat Meters Installed in Consumers'
System
The payment for heating can be counted by heat meters, which can improve the consumer's
consciousniess lo save energy.
in one vord, the proposed project is advanced in technology anid reasonable in design.



5.2 Investigation and Assessment on the Air Pollution
Sources
5.2.1 Investigation into the Air Pollution Sources
5.2.1.1 Purpose of the Investigation
The main aim of the air pollution source investigation is:
*  indicate the number, pLane and vertcal distibution of the air polution soues in the EIA
scope, show the amount of coal-consumption and emissions of various pollutant (including
the heating and non-hcating period)
* reckon the number of the pollution sources to be rcplaced and the discharge amount of
pollutant to be cut by the construction project,,
* state the present environmental qualty and provide the datum basis for evaluating ihe
positive effect by the construction of the project,
*  on the basis of above work, some scientific evidences will be provided  to the project
design and its proposed environmental benefits.
5.2.1.2 Time and Scope of the nvestigation
Time: May to June in 1996; Scope: District Zhifu of Yantai City
Content of the Investigation
A. Number of Boilers in Industry and Enterptises
There are 448 industial and entexprises' boilers in all in District Zhifu, in-which 12 boilers
have a capacity of more than 20 ton, 11 boilers with capacity of 11 - 20ton, and 419 boilers in
the range of 2 - 10 ton, 6 boilers have a capacity 1.4 to 2 ton each. The total tonnage of all the
boilers is 3,030ton/h.
B. Civil-used Kitchen Range
According to our investigafion, the total number of small dispersed boiless, furnaces,
hot-water boilers, kichener ranges in dining room and restaurants is 2,353, and the number of the
boilers with capacity of arround of 1 ton is 289. All of them use coal as fuel. Above Al there are
still 63,000 civil used stove for heating in the area.
C. On the Installation of Stacks
Among all the industrial and enterprises' boilers, 9 boilers have stacks higher than 50mn, 15
with stacks with a height of 40-50mn, 153 with stacks with a height of 30-39m, 97 stacks with
height of 20-29m, 20 stacks lower than 20nm The stack of the civil-used furnaces is lower than
15m.
D. The Way of Boilers' Combustion
Many of the boilers are traveling grate stocker boiler, and the others include reciprocating
grate, double buniung grate and boiling boiler. Coal is the main fuel (Feicheng coal and Datec ,
coal). Cyclone Dedusting ( efficiency: 80%) is mostly used in the boilers. Most boilers havc ,lO
desulfuiziig equipments except those Paper-making Factory with an efficiency of 20%. Only a
t. I



few enterprises have water-film or electric dedusting facilities, whose efficiency is 90--95%. The
civil-uscd fumnaces liave no dedusting anid dCsuIfurizing 1acilitics.
E. The Amount of Coal Consumption
The coal consumption in industry and enterprises in District Zhifu is 1,340,500 tori, in
which 132,100 ton is used for heating. The amount of civil-used coal is 158,900 ton, in which
84, 100 ton is used for heating. The construction project will reduce the coal for space heating by:-
216,000 ton.
F. Emission of Air Pollutants
28,615 ton of SO2, and 6,541 ton of dust are given off from the industrial and enterprises'
boilers, in which 4,228 ton of S02 and 1,057 ton of dust are given off from the coal combustion
for space heating. The civil-uscd stove to be replaced by the construction project emit 5,085 ton
of SO2, 6,356 ton of dust, in which 2,692 ton of S02 and 3,364 ton of dust arise from coal
combustion for space heating.
In District Zhifu of Yantai City, the yearly enmtted amount of S02 is 33,704t, the amount of
dust given off by coal combustion is 12,897t. The annual amount of SO2 from space heating is
6,920t, and dust 4,421t.
5.2.1.4 The Investigation Results
See the EIA report of Yantai 500 Heating Network.
.5.2.2 Assessment on the Air Pollution Sources
The air pollution in the area comes mainly from the enterprises' boilers and the dispersed
civil-uscd stoves, the entcrprises' boilers give rise to more air pollution. The investigation shows
that key air pollution sources (capacity more than 20 ton/h) are distributed in Yantai Municipal
Power Station (4 boilers), Yantai Municipal Paper-
making Factory (3 boilers), Chlorine Soda Plant (2 boilers), and Yantai Municipal Synthetic
Leather Factoiy (3 boilers). Their total tomnage is up to 1515t/h.
17 enterprises use relatively more coal. The yearly total amount of coal used in the 17
enterprises is 1,068,000 ton, 79.970%o of the coal consumption of all enterpnrses.
The detailed rcsults of assessmcnt on the kcy pollution sources are shown in Table 5.2.1. it
shows that the main air pollutant in the assessment area is SO2, whose isostandard pollution
charge accounts for 92.011%, and that of dust accounts for 7.99% . The results suggest that
dedusting devices are installed in most boilers and can operate well, while the boilers'
desulfurizing is still a big problem in this area. The key pollution sources in the assessment area
are the stacks of the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat and Power Station, they contribute 75.8% of the total
pollution. Therefore, it is clear that the desulfurizang and dedusting efficiency in the Huang-Bo-
Hai Heat and Power Station play an important role in air quality improvement in the area.

5.2.3 Analysis on the Change of Air Pollution Sources before and after
Construction of the Project
As mentioned in the Analysis of the Project, the construction unit will purchase
steam from CHP plant of the Huang-Bo-I-lai Hcat and Power Company as its heat
source, keep the three existing regional boilers, and build a new heat load heating boiler
house. The district heating will be realized in this way. Implementation of the proposed
project will remove 290 dispersed heating boilers in the urban area, and reduce some
coal consumption in 21 boilers (for example, 85% of coal consumption will be cut down
in the three existing regional boilers after operation of the proposed project), replaces
289 boilers with capacity of ca. I ton. All the 63,000 civil-used furnaces will also be
eliminated. Analysis on the change of air pollution sources before and after
implementation of the project is shown in Table 5.2.2.
It can be seen that construction of the project will dccrease- the air pollution
emissions in District Zhifu, so it has much environmental benefit.
The Table also reveals that implementation of the project can rcduce ycarly coal
consumption from 1,499,400 ton to 1,305,400 ton, coal consumption decreases by
13%, yearly SO2 and dust emissions are decreased from 33,704 t to 26,896 ton and
from 12,897 t to 8,494 ton separately, the cutting ratio are by 20.20% and 34.14%
respectivcly, 64.73% of the industrial boilers will be removed, and ali the civil-used
furnaces will be eliminated. Although the coal consumption cut down is not so igh, but
the cut down coal is originally combusted in the way of low heat efficiency, low
dedusting efficiency and no desulfurizing device, its SO2 and dust emission is rather large;
above all the boilers to be removed distribute mainly in urban area with dense
population, while the boilers to be added or kept are all in the industrial zone, the overall
factors are expected to ameliorate the air quality greatly in the urban area after
construction of the project.
The Table also shows that implementation of the proposed project decreases the
emissions of air pollutants in Zhifu District, which not only obeys the national regulations
on controlling the total amount of pollution emission in economically developed zones,
severcly polluted zones and environmentally sensitive zones, but also leaves quite
environmental tolerance to the area. Therefore, from the view of environmental
protcotion, construction of the project is very beneficial.

5.3 Monitoring and Assessment on the Air Quality
5.3.1 Accumulative Effect of the Emissions from the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat
and Power Company on the Environment
The West of the Pcak Load Heating Boiler to be built is in the same environmental
function zone with the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat and Power Company. All the west industrial
zone in District Zhifu will be affected by the Company (the effect scope of the Company
is 15 kne2). However, dhe boiler to be built and the Huang-Bo-Hai Heal and Power
Company will be managed by two diferent administration departments, so it is
necessary to state the accumulative effect of the emissions from the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat
and Power Company on the environmlit bcfore the project construction. The LiIA
system was not put into use commonly before 1989, and so there is no detailed materials
on the effect of the emissions from the Company on the air quality.
When Line B was built in 1989, Shiandong Provincial D)esign Institute of Eliectric
Power undertook the EIA work, and the Yantai Municipal Environmental Monitoring
Station had a five-day on-site measurements. The monitored results revealed that at
3000m fronm leeward (location of NE and ENE) of tile Company, (he maximums at any
tiMe of S02 and TSP- were 0.3495mg/rn and 1.077mg/m3, the maximums daily
average of S02 and TSP were 0.1625mg/r3 and 0.627mg/r3. According to the EIA
reports of 1989. aflenmplementation of Line B, the accumulative maximums at any time
of S02 and TSP would be up to 0.4297mg/m3 and 0.1.092mg/rn3, Ihe accumulative
maximums of daily average of SO2 and TSP would be 0.2065 mg/m3 and 0.632mg/r3.
Except that the cumulative maximums at any times of 5(:02 is near the .Standard Limits,
all other three indicators werc beyond Standard Limils, for the background values were
over the Standard Limits. Therefore, it was suggested in the EIA reports to improve the
tvo 4 meter high chimneys in Line A during the construction of Line B, in order to
ameliorate ihc background air pollution. In fact, afler tihe two boilers in Line B was put in
to use in 1992 and 1995 respectively, the four boilers of 35t/h in Line A were not used
any longer, while the total amount of coal consumption kept unchanged. Afier water-
filni dust precipitator in the two boilers of 220t/h was replaced by a electrostatic
dedusting device. the four boilers in the I-luang-Bo-I-lai Heat and Power Company, the
emissions from the Company are ali within the standard Limits.
The Yantai Municipal Environrmental Monitoring Station had anotlier five-day on-
site measurements in February 1996 for thc ElIA of the Yantai Harbour Projict. The
measured results showvs that at the Site of New Bridge,3000m from the leeward of the
IlOOm-high and 180rm-high Stacks, the maximums at any times of SO2 was 0.734mg/n3,
and the maximums of daily average of 802 andi TSP were 0.335ing/m3 and 0.796
mg/rn3. The maximums at any times and maximum of daily average for So2, and daily
average concentralion of TSP were all exceeding the Standard limits greatly, showing the
air quality severely deteriorated. According to the pollution source invesligation, the
largest pollution source is the four boilers in the Huang-Bo-Hai Heat and Power
Company, wvhose coal consumplion was increased from 626,600 ton in 1989 to 820,600

5.3.3   Assessment oni the Present Air Quality
5.3.3.1 Assessment Method
The Method of Singular Indicator wil bc used as assessment methods.
5.3.3.2 The Conclusions of Assessment
The assessment results for the specified sites and area are listed in Table 5.3.9 and
5.3.10.
The concentrations of SO2 and TSP in Yantai City in Spring and Winter exceed the
Class 2 limit of National Ambient Air Quality Standard, particularly in Winter, SO2 and
TSP go beyond the Standard limit more greatly. The pollution comes mainly from coal
combustion in industrial production, space heating in Winter and traffic fly dust. The
yearly change of the pollution in the asscssment area is: more severe in Winter, severe in
Spring and Fall, and light in Summer. The pollution's daily trend is: severe in the moming
and noon, light in the afternoon and evening, more light in the night. The space
distribution of pollution extent is: more severe in the West of the City for its densely
concentrated industry, severe in the urban area, and light in the East of the City.

5.4 Monitoring and Assessment of Noise Effect in Present
Environment
5.4.1 Monitoring of Noise in Present Environment
The TOR of the EIA requires that onc monitoring site be setup at ca. 50 m from
each of 41 Heat Power Stations and 2 relay Station, the site be as near to resident area as
possible. The noise in each site was measured one time in day and one time in night. The
measurement method was strictly according to the (( National Regulations for
Environmental Monitoring)) (Noise Part). The detailed distribution of the monitoring
sites is shown in Fig. 5.4.1.
5.4.2 Assessment of Noise Effect
5.4.2.1 Assessment Standard
((National Noise Environmental Standard in Urban Area )) (GB3096-93) was
adoptcd as assessment standard. The Standard Clas6es are distinguished to use in each
site according to the Noise Environmental Function Zone of Yantai City, see Table 5.4.1.

is 7.57%. The yearly frequencies of winddirections are summarized in Table 5.5.1.2. The

November (4.4m/s), and the slowest in August (2.6m/s).

5.5.1.2 Meteorological Features of Pollution
This EIA uses the sounding matenals of January 1996 as major information sources
with other soundings referred.
A. The Wind Ficld Character of Atmosphere
The law of daily change of wind speed: the wind is fast in daytime and slow in night,
fast in Winter and slow in Summer, the fastest in a day is from 12 o'clock to 14 o'clock
and the slowest from 0.o'clock to 2 o'clock. So it's casier to diffuse and dilute the
pollutants in daytime than in the night.
The vertical characters of wind are: from ground level to IOOm high, the prevailing
wind is to the east, and deflects in clockwise with the altitude rising. Above 300m, the
wind is to the south, and in the altitude of 500 to 800m, the wind is to the north. The

B. Temperature Field Character of Atmosphere

atmospheric boundary layer has clear daily changes. A continuous inversion exists from
the sun-falling to sun-rising in the altitude of 0-300m., which disappears until 9 to 10
o'clock. The regional inversion character is inversion in night occuming more firquently
than in daytime, the average inversion layer is thin, and the biggest inversion is 3.2 C

D. Pollution Coefficients
Pollution coefficient is the ratio of wind frequency to speed at every direction. The
statistics on pollution coefficients in every season is shown in Table 5.5.1.2 and Fi
5.5.1.4 The yearly rose-like diagram of pollution coefficients is seen in Fig. 5.5.1.1.
The pollution cocfficients are not even in every direction, the biggest is in S direction,
3.95; the second is 3.58, in SW direction; 0.32 in ENE direction, the smallest, which
suggests that the area in the North and Northeast of the pollution sources will be most
severely polluted.
E. Atmospheric Stability
Atmospheric Stability can shows turbulence activity of air. Mixing and
diffusing of air pollutant in vertical direction depends on the aUnospheric stability.
According to the requirements of HJ/12.2-93, the atmospheric stabilities in the
whole year and every season are defined using P-T method, as shown in Table
5.5.1.8.

F. Joint-frequency of Wind Speed, Wind Direction and Stability
See EIA Report of Yantai 500 Heating Network.
G. Characters of Sea and Land Breeze
According to year-collectively watching matetials, in Yantai, the sea breeze is in N
direction, and land breeze in S direction. The sea breeze often occurs in daytime with
average speed of 2-3th/s, and the land breeze takes place in night at 1-3m/s.
In Winter, sea breeze appears at 10 to 12, and its direction change from south to
north or north south, and becomes weak until 16 o'clock. The land breeze begins at 20
o'clock in the direction of SW.
In Summer, sea breeze occurs at 7 to 19 o'clock, and begins to change from SW to
NW or N, becomes the strongest at 10 to 16 o'clock, and then weakens and change
direction to S or SW, the land breeze is then forned.
The watching results suggest that the Sea Land Breeze can not cause secondaty air
pollution in the assessment area.

* The prevailing wind in the assessment area is SW, and the second is N. The region to
the north and south of the pollution source will be more severely polluted by the proposed
procct. Thcrefore, the life and the sensitive areas should be arranged to the west of the
pollution sources to lessen the pollution.
* An inversion layer less than 300 m thick near ground appears in the assessment area
at fine breezy night, and is the strongest at 2 to 6 o'clock. Generally, the inversion is the
highest after midnight, which will depress the vertical diffusion of air pollutant from the
highly located sources, and is not good for the pollutant to distantly difflse.
* The local mixed layer is more ffian lOOOm above ground except in Summer night
(near 800m), so compared to the 80 m high stack, it is quite high. Therefore, the
reflection of the mixed layer to the pollutant will not increase the pollution concentration
near ground, but is good for increase the concentration far from the ground.
* The sea land breeze in Yantai is too weak to formn a closed vertical circuit. So it can
not result in secondary pollution.
* Yantai has no sand storm, and its yearly sand-fly day is less than 1, fog time is less
than 20 days, the shortest in the Peninsula However, it has the most precipitation in
Shandong. Compared with the inland area at the sane altitude, Atmosphere in Yantai has
stronger self-cleaning ability.
5.5.2 Calculation on the Air Pollution Concentration from Point
Sources and Its Assessment
5.5.2.1 Calculated Coefficients
According to the results of the analysis on the project, the calculated coefficients of
air pollution are SO2 and TSP.
5.5.2.2 The Diffusing Model Adopted
The proposed project is in the west head of District Zhifiu in Yantai City, and is 5 km
from the urban area. According to the local terrain and topology, the diffusing model of
plain area is used. To eliminate the effect of urban area on the air pollutant transportation,
necessawy corrections is made to the diffusing parameters in the modeL The concentration
of SO2 and TSP will be forecast using the Gauss Gas ModeL See Annex 1.
5.5.2.3  Selection and Correction of the Parameters
A. Selection of the Diffusing Parameters
For details, see EIA Report of Yantai 500 Heating Network.
B. Correction of the Diffusing Parameters
According to the relative regulations of Guideline for EIA (HJ/IT2.1-23.-93).

E. The Results of Atmospheric Inpact Assessment
The assessment methods are: add the calculated Cmax of Daily Average
Conientration and the Cmax of Concentration at any Times to the corresponding
background level concentration and get two sums; then compare the sums to
corresponding Standard Limit; thus reckon the specific value, contribution coefficient and
increment coefficient. and assess them. The assessment results are listed in Table 5.5.2.5
to Table 5.5.2.8.
a) Ground level concentration at any Times along the Axis Line
For SO2
In Winter, the sum of the Cniax at any times of the background and calculated goes
beyond the Standard Limit> The maximum of the specific value is 1.82, occurring in
-Iarbour Site. However, in this site, the contribution coellicient of the proposed project is
only 0.024, and in the sites of l#. 4# and 5#, are only 0.101, 0.044 and 0.034, all lower
than 0.112. Therefore, -it is clear that the sum of SOz concentrations in these sites
exceeding the Standard Limits results from the high background level-concentration.
In Spring, the sums of Cmax at any times of the background and calculated are
wthin the Standard Limit at all the sites except Site 1. lhe  iaxunum of the specific
values is 1.034, occurring in Site 1 (No. 107 Hospital), while the proposed project
contributes only 0.101 to the pollution of this site. The increment coefficient is lower than
0.112, showing that the sum in this site exceeding the Standard Limit arises from the high
background level concentration of SO.
For TSP
In W'inter, all the sums of the Cmax at any times of the background and the
calculated are within the Standard Limit, in which the maximum of the specific values is
0.800, occuring in the Site of New Bridge. The contribution coefficients and the
increment coefficients of the proposed project in all the sites are lower than 0.011
respectively.
In Spring, all the sums of the Cmax at any times of the background and the
calculated are also within the Standard Limit, in which the maxinum  of the specific
values is 0.724, occurring in the Site of No. 107 Hospital. The contribution coefficients
and the increment coefficients of the proposed project in all the sites are lower than 0.011
5-36



respectively.
b) Daily Average Concentration
For SO2
As shown in thc Table, in Wintcr, all the sums of Cmax of the background and the
calculated  exceed the Standard limit. The maximum of the specific values is 2.327,
occurring in Site 4, while the contribution coefficient of the proposed project to the sum
is only 0.011, and those to other sitcs are all lower than 0.071, and the increment
coefficients of the proposed project to the all the sites are less than 0.071. Hence that the
all sums exceed the Standard Limnit is owing to the exceeding the limits of the
background.
The sums of the Cmax of the background and the calculated in Spring are a little
lower than those in Winter. However, except Site 4, the sums on the other sites go
beyond the Standard Limit in Spring. The maximum of the Specific Values is 1.76,
occurring in Site 5. The contfibution coefficient of the proposed project to this site is
0.019. The contribution coefficients and increment coefficients in the other sites are
lower than 0.071 and0.076 respectively.
For TSP
In Winter, as shown in the Table, all the sums of Cmax of the background and the
calculated exceed the Standard Limit. The maximum of the specific values is 2.010,
occuring in Site 1, while the contribution coefficient of the proposed project to the sum
is only 0.005, those to other sites are all lower than 0.005, . Hence that the all sums
exceed the Standard Limit is owing to that the background level concentrations go
beyond the linits .
In Spring, except Site 3, the sums on the other sites go beyond the Standard lnimit.
The maximum of the Specific Values is 2.010, occurring in Site 1. The contribution
coeffici'.nt of the proposed project to this site is 0.005. The contribution coefficients and
the increment coefficients in the other sites are lower than 0.005 and 0.005 respectively.
5.5.3 Environmental Impact Assessment on Pollution Sources
to be Replaced by the Proposed Project
5.5.3.1 Assessment Pollutants
SO2 and TSP.
5.5.3.2 Assessment Scope
The area to be heated by the Heating Network- in District Zhifu of Yantai City. Its
area is 30 k2m
5.5.3.3 Standards Adopted in this Assessment
537



The  ((National Ambient Air Quality Standards)) (GB3095-82) is used in the
assessment. According to Functions of the Zones Divided by Yantai Government, Class 2
of the Standards is suitable to the West Suburb, and Class 1 suitable to the urban central
arca.
5.5.3.4 Calculation Items
llic ground concentration and winterly average concentrations of SO2 and TSP in
the concmrned grids are calculated by using the Model recommended in ((Technical
Guideline of EIA )) HJ I T2.1 - 2.3-93.. The calculated results is compared to the
present concentration, and thus to forecast the positive effect of implementation of the
project.
5.5.3.5 Assessment Method
The pollution sources to be replaced by inplementation of the project is firstly
investigated, and the assessment area is divided in to 500x500 grids, the equivalent
pollution source in each grid is reckoned out. Th1C calculated concentration in each
concerned site is: the- value of subtracting the pollutant's concentration of the replaced
pollution sources from that of the newly added pollution sources.
5.5.3.6 Forecasting the Pollutant's Concentration
A. On the Pollution Sources to be Replaced
The survey shows that implementation of the proposed project wvill eliminate 280
boilers, decrease yearly coal consumption by 132,100 ton; remove 63,000 civil-used
stovcs, and( also decrease yearly coal consumption by 84,100 ton. The total yearly coal
consumption is decreased by 216,200 ton, and thus decrease SO2 emission by 6920 t/y,
and dust emission by 4421 t/y. The detailed infonrnaion are listed in Table 4-1 to Table
4-4. Flronm the Table, it can be secn that the pollution sources to be replaccd cmit at low
altitude, most stacks are lower than 30m (only four with height of 40, three with 35 m
high), the stacks of the civil-used stoves are lower than ISm.
B. G(id Analysis on the Pollution Sources to be Replaced
According to the Aidc Memoir lcft in May by the World bank, the assessmcnt area is
divided into 128 500x500 grids, including 102 grids containing pollution sources, and
26 grids free of pollution sources. The original grid is in the southwest suburb, its location
is seen in Fig. 5.5.3.1 -and Fig. 5.5.3.2.
C. Forecasting of the Ground level concentration of the Pollutants
a) Selcction of the Model
See Annex 1.
b) Selection of Sites for Calculation of Ground level concentration

c) Calculation Results and Analysis
i) On the Ground level conc:entrationi of Pollution
Table 4-37 to Table 4-44 of EIA Report of Yantai 500 heating Network show the
ground level concentrations of SO2 and Dust in each representative grid under conditions
of various Stability and Wind Direction.
The results shows that the ground level concentration gradually increase with the
Stability rising, suggesting that the positive impacts of the proposed project becomes
miore obvious in stable weather. This is because: the pollutants fruin the pollution sources
to be replaced are emitted at low altitude, and the stable weather is unfavorable for them
to diff-use, so the ground level concentration of the pollutants is quite high. Under the
same stability, thle ground level concentration of the pollutant decreases with the wind
speed rising, in accordance to the general laws.
The distribution of the ground level concentration is: in Grids of Harbour and
Worker's Sanitanium with wind directions of NW, NNW, N, rNNE, NE and NNE, the
ground level concentration is lower for less pollution sources existing in these locations; in
Grids of the Bearing Factory and the New World, it's high with the wind directions of
